Notes 2026-07-11 (second run):
- Outbound fetch succeeded this run (contrast with the earlier same-day failure logged above) — 17 of 19 feeds returned usable content. FTC's feed initially 403'd against the descriptive bot UA specified in the runbook; it returned 200 with a standard browser UA, so it is counted as OK, not failed — worth revisiting the UA string if this recurs.
- Selection window: no successful collection ran between the July 9 23:30 ET baseline and this run, so candidates span July 9 15:30 UTC (lastRun minus 12h overlap) through July 11 ~16:20 UTC — about 49 hours folded into one edition. 72 items were reviewed across all responding feeds; 12 passed the relevance gate (EDITORIAL §3) and were admitted (no pending state).
- Verification pass (EDITORIAL §7) caught 6 claims that outran their cited excerpts and stripped each to what the excerpt actually supports, across 13 edit locations (wire/diffPool/dossier-event/prose copies of the same claim): (1) linking the CitrixBleed2 initial-access-broker item to "NetScaler" and "first flagged July 6" — not stated in today's fetched excerpt, so the product-name and date linkage were dropped; (2) labeling the new Balbooa Forms / iCagenda CISA KEV entries "Joomla extensions" — only Balbooa's own notes URL supports that, iCagenda's does not, so the label was dropped for both; (3) calling Gitea a "widely used" Git-hosting tool in the cyber assessment — not in the excerpt, changed to "self-hosted" (which is); (4)-(5) a "without waiting for a patch" / "rather than wait for a patch" clause on the ShareFile item (lead why-line and takeaway) — patch status isn't stated in the source, dropped both times; (6) calling the Woodinville DOJ defendant a "bank employee" in the insider assessment — the source says "financial institutions," changed to match. No item was cut outright; 0 of 12 drafted items were dropped, well under the one-third failure threshold.

It was not backfilled today, since the runbook's selection window is forward-looking from `lastRun` and backfilling missed items is a deliberate correction action under EDITORIAL §9, not a default of a forward run. Flagging for a human decision on whether to add it as a correction.
- Friday, July 10 produced no weekly digest: that date's only activity was editorial-only edits (no collection ran), so the runbook's "Fridays: prepend a weekly digest" step never fired. `meta.nextWeekly` advanced from the already-elapsed "Fri, Jul 10" to "Fri, Jul 17"; no digest was backfilled for the missed week.
